  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_31555d6f-36a2-4613-b817-35f767d8659b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<div id="review_1909305491" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1909305491" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2981934596869190505">I grow to love Royce & Hadrian more and more as I read the books. These two characters are just so wonderful and I feel they fit together nicely as best friends and family. ♥<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487607069i/22031364._SX540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Even when one is mad with the other they just get it done and get over it. =)<br/><br/><b>

We aren't going to do that again, are we?"<br/>Hadrian said miserably. "I've been sitting in cold water for hours. I'll cramp."<br/><br/>"You know another w</blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText2981934596869190505" style="display:none">I grow to love Royce &amp; Hadrian more and more as I read the books. These two characters are just so wonderful and I feel they fit together nicely as best friends and family. ♥<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487607069i/22031364._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even when one is mad with the other they just get it done and get over it. =)<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"You ready?" Royce asked. <br>"For what?"<br>"Turn around. Let's go back-to-back and link arms."<br>"You're kidding. We aren't going to do that again, are we?"<br>Hadrian said miserably. "I've been sitting in cold water for hours. I'll cramp."<br><br>"You know another way to get up there?" Royce asked, and Hadrian shook his head. Royce looked up. "It isn't even as high as the last time and it's narrower, so it'll be easier. Stand up and stretch a second. You'll be fine."<br><br>"What if the guard is up there with a stick to poke us with?"<br><br>"Do you want to get out of here or not?"<br><br>Hadrian took a deep breathe. "I'm still mad at you," he said, turning and linking arms back-to-back with Royce.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>•••••••<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Weapons?" Hadrian asked. <br>"I'll check the house. You see about getting horses."<br>"Don't kill anyone," Hadrian mentioned. <br>"I'll try not to, but if I see Luret--"<br>"Oh yeah, kill him."</blockquote>
</b><br><br>In this book they are trying to help Arista get some things done, win some people over so they can fight the bigger enemy. <br><br>Arista put on her big girl panties and got down to the nitty gritty with the boys even though she's royalty and I loved her spunk and lovely attitude through-out the book. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Just a few questions I thought you would be able to shed some light on," Royce told him. "Why don't we talk in your study while Hadrian and Arista get out of their wet things? Is it all right if we spend the night here?"<br><br>"Certainly. I'll have dinner brought up, although you picked a bad day; the kitchen is serving meat pies." He made a grimace. <br><br>Arista stood stiffly, feeling her heart still racing. She narrowed her eyes and glared. "I hate all of you."</blockquote>
</b><br><br>There are some revelations that Hadrian learns about when they all go back to his homeland. Now he feels he needs to go on his own quest but he wanted to do something like that before. <br><br>Royce has his own mind set on a different life too and it makes me happy. BUT, they better not split up and they better keep going on in other books. And then be friends and hang out forever. lol <br><br>Some people I liked died in the book but that is a given. <br><br>Either way, I just love this book. I love the camaraderie between the boys. I love the other people that are in the books. Arista, Gwen, Esrahaddon, Modina and many more. There is a whole other part of the book dedicated to Modina but I didn't want to talk too much about her for reasons. I do wonder about her and if she's something else entirely. <br><br>Anyway, I loved the book! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487607977ra/22031473.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm so hoping Michael J. Sullivan doesn't kill the boys later on! I always dread moving on to the next book for that fear! AND NO ONE TELL ME IF HE DOES, unless of course he doesn't then that's okay. lol<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/02/rise-of-empire-by-michael-j-sullivan.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_1234019290" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1234019290" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1234019290?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fae">fae</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1234019290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2806073265090065356"><b>Brilliant.</b><br/>Brilliant <b>plotline</b>. Brilliant <b>pace</b>. Brilliant <b>characters</b>. Brilliant <b>world-building</b>. Brilliant <b>plot twists</b>.<br/><b>Brilliant everything.</b><br/>All hail Master Sullivan!<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There are no honorable causes. There is no good or evil. Evil is only what we call those who oppose us.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>The New Empire is rising. The Church uses a half-mad fake empress to unite the Realms of Men in the name of Novron. War is raging between the imperial armies and Melengar, the only Avryn kingdom that still resists, while </span>
  <span id="freeText2806073265090065356" style="display:none"><b>Brilliant.</b><br />Brilliant <b>plotline</b>. Brilliant <b>pace</b>. Brilliant <b>characters</b>. Brilliant <b>world-building</b>. Brilliant <b>plot twists</b>.<br /><b>Brilliant everything.</b><br />All hail Master Sullivan!<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There are no honorable causes. There is no good or evil. Evil is only what we call those who oppose us.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />The New Empire is rising. The Church uses a half-mad fake empress to unite the Realms of Men in the name of Novron. War is raging between the imperial armies and Melengar, the only Avryn kingdom that still resists, while the Nationalist rebels under the leadership of Degan Gaunt oppose the Church's strive for world domination. And a swordsman and a thief have the potential to stop their devious schemes. Or doom the world.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You must choose between darkness and light,a nd your choice will affect many.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />You may wonder why you should read Riyria while there are so many fantasy books out there, each of them narrating a different version of the constant battle between Good and Evil. The answer is simple: Mr.Sullivan's world of fantasy is unique, beautiful, breathtaking and absolutely, undoubtedly <b>EPIC</b>.<br /><br />Why?<br />-Mr.Sullivan is excellent at <b>manipulation</b>. You don't know who is going to betray whom, who is an ally and who is a foe, and when you think you get a clear picture, your beliefs are turned upside down. During <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790277.Rise_of_Empire__The_Riyria_Revelations___2_" title="Rise of Empire (The Riyria Revelations, #2) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Rise of Empire</a>, I was deceived, cheated and in the end, I stood wide eyed and my mouth hung open because I could not come to terms with what I just read.<br />-As contradictory as it may sounds, surprises isn't the only weapon in Mr.Sullivan's arsenal. He left enough <b>hints</b> for the reader to sense an impending doom, a catastrophe that will change Hadrian and Royce's lives forever, but you can do nothing to stop it, just wait helpless and see. And that's even more painful than the plot twists.<br />-<b>Royce and Hadrian.</b> They are an unpredictable pair, some of the greatest heroes that I have ever encountered. Hadrian is noble, tired of serving the highest bidder, he searches a greater purpose in his life. Royce on the other hand, is <i>practical</i> and doesn't care about morality or justice. But as his walls crumble, as we get a better perspective of the way he grew up, the lack of family and a place where he belongs, my heart breaks for him. Both Hadrian and Royce are painted so vividly that I can't help but feel that I have known them my entire life.<br />-<b>The female characters.</b> I love their courage and strength and resourcefulness. Arista has turned from a spoiled princess into a fighter, a witch and a politician, a woman who takes her fate in her own hands and proves that she is no longer a damsel in distress. Thrace and Amilia are also great, but the biggest surprise for me is Gwen. Who thought that a prostitute would be a gentle, wise and caring woman, whose affection and kindness would soften the toughest thief?<br />-<b>Merrick.</b> I hate him with a loathing passion, but he is cunning and a genious villain. The way he played Riyria is both frustrating and fascinating.<br />-And of course there are the epic <b>battles</b>, the interesting secondary characters, the spells, the warnings and a whole new world full of <b>adventures</b> and <b>dangers</b>. And <b>goblins</b>.<br /><br />Need I say more?</span>
  <a data-text-id="2806073265090065356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1788924265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1788924265" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1788924265?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10803593-rise-of-empire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=self-published-and-indie">self-published-and-indie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1788924265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17514733901609715488">It’s safe to say now that with each installment, each book in the series certainly gets better in its quality consistently. The 2nd omnibus in Riyria Revelations titled Rise of Empire consists of book 3, Nyphron Rising and book 4, The Emerald Storm and it's a superior omnibus by far compared to the previous omnibus, Theft of Swords. Like my Theft of Swords review, I’ll start my review after showing you another beautiful book cover done right by Marc Simonetti and a beautiful fanart of a scene in</span>
  <span id="freeText17514733901609715488" style="display:none">It’s safe to say now that with each installment, each book in the series certainly gets better in its quality consistently. The 2nd omnibus in Riyria Revelations titled Rise of Empire consists of book 3, Nyphron Rising and book 4, The Emerald Storm and it's a superior omnibus by far compared to the previous omnibus, Theft of Swords. Like my Theft of Swords review, I’ll start my review after showing you another beautiful book cover done right by Marc Simonetti and a beautiful fanart of a scene in The Emerald Storm.<br><br><b>Nyphron Rising</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485260788i/21797688._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Fanart of Royce &amp; Hadrian scaling <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the Tower of Drumindor <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485260788i/21797689._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The plot-lines from the two books in Rise of Empire are much more engrossing than before. Whether it’s from book 3 or book 4, the series keeps building upon the event that happened in the previous book carefully. <b>It still doesn’t reach the “epic fantasy” scope at this point but more intriguing events and themes such as civil war, pirates, politics, loyalty, friendship and love can be found here.</b> The plot itself this time are connected with our main character’s, Royce and Hadrian’s background which in previous installments are clearly withhold and made their characteristic flat as a board, not this time. After finding out more about their history, it’s more interesting to see how the story will develop from their POV and even though the plot in each book are still predictable to me, <b>I really can’t predict how the overarching and main plot of the series will conclude, especially who the Heir of Novron is.</b> There’s so much foundation being lay upon from these 4 books and I hope Michael managed to conclude it brick by brick on the conclusion.<br><br>World-building are expanded more and Michael's writing is still very easy to read. There are some parts on the world-building aspect that bothers me though, in my opinion there’s way too many unnecessary names to remembered, whether it’s from place, lore and characters. Now, this is usually a good thing since it means the world, history and lore are richer in content but there are too many characters which were introduced only in each book and never to be seen again. It kills the motivation to remember most of them since you’ll probably know that some of the minor characters introduced probably won’t make an appearance again after what happened in the respective installment. I could care less about what happened to them since the amount of buildup done towards them are really scarce.<br><br>Although the writing are still easy to read, but seeing Michael wrote all 6 book before publishing any of them, I find there’s no improvement at all on its writing. This is my personal opinion, it’s probably one of the two factors that will never work with me throughout this series and I have to look past it to enjoy these books more, the narrative. I mentioned before that I simply can’t care about Royce &amp; Hadrian since I find the narrative robbed them of their motivation and feelings, this still remained true. I'm used to it already but it's just a shame I can't get attached to the characters since we never get to be inside their heads, I even find 1st person POV which usually doesn't sit well with me to be better in comparison.<br><br>Even though I can’t attach myself to the characters in this series, it doesn’t mean that they’re not a great character. In fact, Hadrian &amp; the other main’s character POV are so interesting and addictive to read, especially the girls in this series, Arista, Modina and Amilia. It’s stunning how much development were put into the girls story line, I find them to be a superior written characters compared to Royce, especially Arista. Her POV and character development from book 1 are simply amazing, that’s all I’ll say on this subject. It's really better for you to see their developments for yourself but if you’re looking for a high fantasy series with a great and strong female characters, rest assured you can find them here. Michael proved to us that it's possible to write strong female characters without them having any weapons at their disposal.<br><br>Yes, you heard that right, the main problem with Royce for me from before still remained and at this point, I just have to put it in my mindset that Royce was a “badass” in the past but he’s just smart and fast in the present. If I'm proven wrong in the last books then I'll be happy but as of now, there are way too many times the characters in the book mentioned something like Royce is a legend, he can kill everyone and all that and I get it already, he’s an amazing assassin in the past <i>(which we didn’t get to see in actions)</i>, now please let me see he live his legends in the present please?? And by actions what I meant is not only one or two time occurrence like in these two books which happened only in a few pages. Luckily this case doesn’t hold true for Hadrian, my new favorite out of the two. <b>For a kind-hearted to a fault character, Hadrian proved himself to be a beast when needed to be and holds true to his legend.</b> We get to see him in actions a LOT this time and I’m really pleased to read all his POV chapters, starting from his background, all his action scenes, his friendship with Royce and loyalty to his friends and principle.<br><br><b>Hadrian with his Spadone.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485260788i/21797690.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There's another really huge problem I definitely can’t overlook which doesn't affect my rating of this book since it still remained to be seen in the conclusion of the series, I’m really hoping with all my heart I would be proven wrong. One of the character in the book, I won’t tell you who, explicitly foreshadowed the character itself that he/she will die. This is a seriously stupid decision if it ended up happening, the character and narrative basically spoiled the plot twist and killed the surprising factor itself. For those of you who have read the book or series, I’m talking about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Gwen <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. This is still inconclusive but I have a feeling from the stories predictability until now that it will end up happening.<br><br>Although some problems from previous omnibus still persist here, overall, I find Rise of Empire to be a much better and more engrossing experience if you can look beyond some of its flaws. I can ALMOST safely recommend this series to anyone who’s looking for a lighter high fantasy series to read, I have to read the conclusion of the series first before truly recommending it to anyone. However, I can confirm that everyone's statement about the series being better with its next sequel is true. I gave the first book, Crown Conspiracy a mere 2 stars, it’s basically one of the lowest book I ever rated, look how I rated this omnibus and see for yourself how the series grow consistently and I hope the end will prove to be as satisfying as everyone keep on telling me.<br><br><b>
  <i>Nyphron Rising: 4/5 Stars<br>The Emerald Storm: 4/5 Stars<br><br>Rise of Empire: 8/10 Stars</i>
</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17514733901609715488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1612033427" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1612033427?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1612033427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4278382272876307988"><b>Re-read with some friends at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a> 7/12/19</b><br/><br/>2nd read and the book holds up mostly. The 3rd book is more of a political maneuvering plot line and while the set up is great I missed some of the action of the other books. The 4th book though is a swashbuckling adventure and the boys are back at everything they do best. I might drop this half a star to 4.5 stars, but overall great even on a second read.<br/><br/>Original Review:<br/><br/><b>
  <a>Buddies Books & Baubles</a>
</b> Buddy read 4/18/16.......the Royce a</span>
  <span id="freeText4278382272876307988" style="display:none"><b>Re-read with some friends at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a> 7/12/19</b><br><br>2nd read and the book holds up mostly. The 3rd book is more of a political maneuvering plot line and while the set up is great I missed some of the action of the other books. The 4th book though is a swashbuckling adventure and the boys are back at everything they do best. I might drop this half a star to 4.5 stars, but overall great even on a second read.<br><br>Original Review:<br><br><b>
  <a>Buddies Books &amp; Baubles</a>
</b> Buddy read 4/18/16.......the Royce and Hadrian bromance continues.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460981605ra/18809445.gif" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“There are no honorable causes. There is no good or evil. Evil is only what we call those who oppose us.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Michael J Sullivan (MJS): Do you like adventures?<br><br>Me: <i>Yes….I do like a tale with a good adventure or quest in it.</i><br><br>(MJS): Do you like a broken hero who doesn’t really want to be the hero?<br><br>Me: <i>Of course that is one of my favorite tropes…the not so good, good guy.</i><br><br>(MJS): What about betrayals, double-crosses, plots and pirates?<br><br>Me: <i>The more the better I say as long as there is revenge in the long term for the good guys.</i><br><br>(MJS): And three dimensional Female characters that aren’t just looking for someone to love them. How do you feel about those?<br><br>Me: <i>Hmmm….well yes I do like them. But there is some kissing right? I mean I don’t need a lot but I love to have something to ship and a smidgen of romance to go with all the betraying, double-crossing and pirates.</i><br><br>(MJS): Okay, yes there are a few kisses in this. But this is in no way a kissing book.<br><br>Me: <i>Alright this seems like it might be something I like. What about the villain, is he/she any good?</i><br><br>(MJS): I think you mean villain(s) plural and each is fantastic in their own way and each has his/her own motivations.<br><br>Me: <i>This is sounding better all the time. Okay I must read this because I did love the Bromance between Royce and Hadrian in the first book. This sounds even better.</i><br><br><b>…….2 days later.</b><br><br>Me: Michael it was so much better. I loved what you did there with Royce and Hadrian. Sure this was more of a political book in the first half but I enjoyed the new dynamic of their team after Hadrian finds out about his secret destiny.<br><br>Also you have some great bad guys. It was hard for me to pick just one to hate since there are quite a few to pick from. Everything from just a general thugs, to a religious fanatic bent on power, to a man out for revenge against the one he thinks wronged him years ago. Well done on that front. I’m going to say that I was partial to Merrick though since he seems the most dangerous of the lot.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“You think you’re a very clever fellow, don’t you?” Saldur challenged.<br>“No, Your Grace,” Merrick replied. “Clever is the man who makes a fortune selling dried-up cows, explaining how it saves the farmers the trouble of getting up every morning to milk them. I’m not clever—I’m a genius.”</i>
</blockquote><br>That you are Mr. Merrick….I knew he was clever and playing a dangerous game and he still fooled me all the way.<br><br>You didn’t go light on Thrace though did you.<br><br>(MJS): You didn’t think she’d be safe after the events of the last book did you?<br><br>Me: <i>Well, no not exactly. But I definitely didn’t think it would start to go that bad for her either. I do love all the stuff you did to and with her character though. Just when I though I knew what was going on in her head….you proved that I didn’t know anything.</i><br><br>(MJS): Did you find the ship you were looking for?<br><br>Me: YES!!!! And then you know what happened. But there was just enough kissing in this to keep that girly part of my head and heart happy.<br><br>But do you want to know one of my favorite parts was????<br><br>(MJS): Of Course….was it when the two men boiled from the inside out?<br><br>Me: Oh…you do know me well and I very much enjoyed when they got what was coming to them but no it was much later. I totally loved the arena type battle that Hadrian, Royce and a few others went through. It reminded me of my time playing World Of Warcraft PvP (player vs player) arena battles. So great.<br><br>(MJS): I see you have a bloodthirsty side to go with the ‘girly parts’ of you. <br><br>Me: I enjoyed this so much….there was action, intrigue, kissing, battles and a plethora of great dialogue. Plus it seems that Merrick knows a Royce that was much different than the man he is today. I wonder what he is going to do to Merrick when they finally meet up again….I think it might get a little bloody.<br><br>(MJS): No spoilers from me. <br><br>Me: Fine…I must go. I have to read the next book because this one was so bloody good. You pleasantly surprised me with the complexity of your story Mr. Sullivan. Thanks for the talk.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4278382272876307988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1764814229" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1764814229" />
    <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna"><img alt="Lady Luna. ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575639837p2/53385361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1764814229?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Luna. ✨" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna">Lady Luna. ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=great-books">great-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=badassery">badassery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1764814229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer858078990700369228"><b> 4/5 Stars</b><br/><br/>I really enjoyed reading Rise of Empire, I definitely enjoyed it more then Theft of Swords. This book certainly picked up the pace from book one, seriously <b>interesting things actually happened in this book</b>. The plot was fast paced and stimulating. I believe there was a fair bit of badassery going on. I didn't even notice the weird emotionless POV much this time, like yeah it was obviously still there, <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472968907ra/20371981.gif' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/> but it's more bearable because I've finally warmed up to the characters. <br/><br/><b>This still</b></span>
  <span id="freeText858078990700369228" style="display:none"><b> 4/5 Stars</b><br><br>I really enjoyed reading Rise of Empire, I definitely enjoyed it more then Theft of Swords. This book certainly picked up the pace from book one, seriously <b>interesting things actually happened in this book</b>. The plot was fast paced and stimulating. I believe there was a fair bit of badassery going on. I didn't even notice the weird emotionless POV much this time, like yeah it was obviously still there, <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472968907ra/20371981.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br> but it's more bearable because I've finally warmed up to the characters. <br><br><b>This still isn't my favourite 'bromance' ever, I really like Royce and Hadrian and enjoy their banter. But for me the bromance just isn't there yet, like I feel I'm missing something. ARE WE READING THE SAME BOOK?!?</b> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441876713i/16163468._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br> Once again this book is two novels in one. This time around we get <b>Nyphron Rising</b> and <b>The Emerald Storm. </b>All stories are a continuation of each other with a connected plot, so it flows really well. <br>Michael J Sullivan is a fantastic writer, his books are easy to read, his a great vivid world-builder and its definitely a humorous and fun read. <br>I found the pacing better in this instalment then Theft of Swords, the overall storyline was once again unoriginal but good. In my opinion this book was a little more my cup tea. Theft of Swords was very "classic" fantasy, it didn't have much violence. Whereas this book Rise of Empire was a little more dark, we got to read about the darker side to Royce, Hadrian and Arista. I really enjoyed the overall vibe in this book, we witnessed a few brutal barbaric acts like floggings and the fight scenes which might I add were next level to what I saw in book one, they were fantastic, <i>a certain fight scene was so amazing, I was on the edge of seat while reading it, while having heart palpitations, </i>so yeah that was pretty fun. This book was also more complex then the first, it had a few major twists, aswell as castle intrigue, court politics, love and relationship secrets, *sounds of amazement* finally getting some good stuff out of Michael J Sullivan's novels. Its definitely safe to say I'm a fan of <i>The Riyria</i> and want more! I can't wait to finish the series.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486345247i/21906172._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Seriously I love Arista so much. I just low key wish I was her so I could turn people into frogs.<br><br>I didn't like <b>Nyphron Rising</b> as much as The Emerald Storm, only because it wasn't as action packed, other then that it was a really good book. I liked it a lot. I love Arista so was happy to have a story with her POV, as one of the main POV's. This story is set a year after the last book, and is basically about the beginning of a war. Hadrian and Royce are now both retired but go on their 'last mission' (they're always saying, every mission is their last lol). Arista sets off on a mission to save her brothers empire and takes Hadrian and Royce with her. The story was thrilling and engaging enough, I just wanted more action?! Luckily The Emerald Storm delivered me a lot of violence so I'm now a happy camper.<br><br>My favorite out of the two stories was definitely <b>The Emerald Storm</b>, it was so EPIC. This book is what I was waiting for, seriously thank you Michael J Sullivan for finally showing me your potential as an author, this book definitely exceeded my expectations and I loved it! Seriously, it was so bloody good. It was your typical action packed Pirate story, we follow Royce and Hadrian as they go on a journey to find an object. Of course the journey doesn't go to plan and they find themselves in a deadly location. <b>The rumours are definitely true folks, this series gets better with each book</b>. The twists and reveals at the end were mind blowing and <b>IT ACTUALLY HAD AWESOME FIGHT SCENES</b>. This was an action packed, fun, exhilarating book that I absolutely loved reading and I just need to fangirl over Hadrian, Royce &amp; Arista. Seriously they are all awesome. I really missed Myron this story but found Hadrian's POV to be my relief this time around. I really love Hadrian now, he is so amazing, clumsy, funny, dopey and he is very badass and handsome. Definitely swoon worthy, when he withdrew his Spadone sword shit got hectic and a lot of people died(yayayayaya). But I can't chose if I like him more then Royce or not. Royce definitely had a few standout badass moments in these books and I have a new level of respect for him. <b>
  <i>"Oh, sir, you have no idea what Royce is like. I'll grant you that his association with Hadrian Blackwater has tempered him greatly. Twelve years with that idealistic dreamer have made him practically human, but I know him. I know what lurks beneath. I've seen things that make even my hardened heart shudder. Get his anger up, and you'll unleash a demon that no one can control. Believe me, he's like that and so much more. Nothing is beyond him"</i>
</b><br><br>I recommend this book to all fantasy lovers. Although I must say if you are looking for a blood bath or a high violence fantasy, then keep on looking this is a more humorous soft fantasy, with classic themes. Definitely a fun filled read that I'm sure most fantasy fans would love.<br><br><b>
  <i>Nyphron Rising</i>
</b> - <b>3.5/5</b><br><b>
  <i>The Emerald Storm</i>
</b> - <b>4.5/5</b> <br><b>Total Rating - 4/5</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="858078990700369228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16659837919911727069">3.5* <br/><br/>The 2nd volume from The Riyria Revelations is better written, has better world building, the dialogue between Royce and Hadrian is still fun. The plot got a bit static in the middle but I still enjoyed reading most of it. This series is easy and fun ,nothing too artistic but it warms you up inside in its best moments. It has a few flaws but all in all I can't wait to read the follow up. <br/><br/>I particularly enjoyed the way Arista character developed, she makes less mistakes than in the first part</span>
  <span id="freeText16659837919911727069" style="display:none">3.5* <br /><br />The 2nd volume from The Riyria Revelations is better written, has better world building, the dialogue between Royce and Hadrian is still fun. The plot got a bit static in the middle but I still enjoyed reading most of it. This series is easy and fun ,nothing too artistic but it warms you up inside in its best moments. It has a few flaws but all in all I can't wait to read the follow up. <br /><br />I particularly enjoyed the way Arista character developed, she makes less mistakes than in the first part of the series, she becomes more complex. In general women are better developed in this volume. </span>

<div id="review_2420449753" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2420449753" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2420449753?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2420449753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15377427243437288205"><b>“What do we do?”<br/>“What we always do,” Royce replied, “only better.”</b><br/><br/>This is an omnibus edition which means that it contains <b>two books</b>, <b>Nyphron Rising</b> and <b>The Emerald Storm</b>. Two books in a dense series mean a whole lot of action, plot-twists, turning points and (un)expected developments. As this is essentially <b>a story-driven tale</b>, there is no point in even trying to give you a teaser what awaits or the essence of what is coming as it would only result in spoilers. <br/><br/>There are <b>two basic ways in which </b></span>
  <span id="freeText15377427243437288205" style="display:none"><b>“What do we do?”<br />“What we always do,” Royce replied, “only better.”</b><br /><br />This is an omnibus edition which means that it contains <b>two books</b>, <b>Nyphron Rising</b> and <b>The Emerald Storm</b>. Two books in a dense series mean a whole lot of action, plot-twists, turning points and (un)expected developments. As this is essentially <b>a story-driven tale</b>, there is no point in even trying to give you a teaser what awaits or the essence of what is coming as it would only result in spoilers. <br /><br />There are <b>two basic ways in which you can read this novel</b>: <br /><br />For a <b>4 star review</b> click here: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />For the first time in years, Riyria have a respectable job and a steady income. Riyria, just to remind you consists of <b>Royce Melborn who regards the law merely as suggestion</b> and violence as means to all ends, and <b>Hadrian Blackwater who breathes principles and dines on honour</b>. The previous instalment focused on <b>bromance</b> between the two. This time, their friendship and, indeed, partnership will be tested by doubts and strife. This makes the <b>dynamic between them more interesting</b>, allows for <b>character development</b> and more <b>nuanced character building</b>. Although it does not mean that there will be no banter or action scenes so those of you who liked the duo will not be disappointed. <br /><br />As the story progresses, more and <b>more protagonists appear</b> and are given voice. Among them, the most prominent are the members of the Melengar royal family, Alric and Arista, the ancient wizard Ezrahaddon and Thrace, upon whom the fortune smiled in a particularly ironic way together with her new companion, Amilia. Those of the readers who were not so impressed with Royce and Hadrian will perhaps be relived to hear that the <b>other characters are given much wider margin to this extent that at times one might get the feeling that Royce and Hadrian are secondary to the main plot</b>. <br /><br />We learn more regarding the Riyria background and their personal stories, but also how their lives fit into other story-arcs and the grand tale of Novron’s heir. We get to know other political forces and get to visit other places on the vast map of this world. You will get battles, and duels, scheming and backstabbing, escapes and rescues (although admittedly some scenes will be familiar). There is also a sea gig (yay or nay? for me a nay, the only maritime story I adored was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2404283932?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fox</a>, and only because it was not defined by this setting). <br /><br />While I enjoyed the book, I could not get over the feeling that the whole tale is told with <b>a hefty dose of naivety</b> that is not entirely thought through. On the one hand, you will have <b>brutality and cruelty</b>, on the other events will play out according to <b>logic that is almost childish</b>. Consequently, while it is a book that I’d hand to a middle grader without any qualms and with words of encouragement, I had to <b>suspend my sarcastic reasoning more than once</b>. If you are a super-down-to-earth reader, some things might be irritating for you. The scenes with Amilia, the simple girl who uses words like “inconveniencing” and “indisposed”, Hadrian taking over command in a military camp <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Mr Sullivan, “I have money”? Really!? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, the antagonists so cliche in their mustache-twirling evilness or heroes going into the battle 2 days after receiving 100 lashes are good examples of those.<br /><br /> If you think too much about certain things, they stop adding up. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Like: it is kind of unclear how humans managed to subjugate races clearly more advanced technologically and magically (elves and dwarves) and more powerful? Or you’ll start questioning the secret knights. Why didn’t they kill the heir immediately when they found him? They were trying to do so for 100 years! Why taking him captive for a change? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Additionally, while the books read fast and are a pleasant read overall, <b>I cannot say that this prose impressed me greatly</b>. In fact, among my notes and highlights, there was not a single sentence I underlined because I liked the sound of it. No profound reflections, no wise observations, no poetry. The writing style is succinct, at times funny in a sitcom-like way but it will not prove you with great quotes or one-liners. <br /><br /><b>The Riryia Revelations are revelational if you are looking for a smart and funny comfort read</b>. Not too overwhelming or ambitious, not too heavy or depressing. Just short of hitting the soft spot. <b>And you know what? It is dedicated to Goodreads members. How could you not give it a try?</b><br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />For a <b>1 star review</b> click here: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />For the first time in years, Riyria have a respectable job and a steady income. Riyria, just to remind you consists of <b>Royce Melborn who regards the law merely as suggestion</b> and violence as means to all ends, and <b>Hadrian Blackwater who breathes principles and dines on honour</b>. Unfortunately for those who were pining for more bromance between those two, <b>other characters are given much wider margin to this extent that at times one might get the feeling that Royce and Hadrian are secondary to the main plot</b>. <br /><br />Among those crown <s>idiot</s> princess Arista takes the precedence. In book three she nearly dominates the whole book and her POV is more frequent and longer than those of Royce and Hadrian combined.<br /><br />The one and only reason why the books, yes both of them, are of the one-star quality, is <b>the unbearable stupidity of princess Arista and her antics</b>. Mind you, she was getting on my nerves before, but it has been nothing when compared with the tomfooleries that await here: <br /><br />1. A princess of the crown after throwing tantrum at the prospect of a strategic marriage goes <b>traipsing around as an ambassador in a dirty carriage and a crumpled dress</b>.<br /><br />2. A princess of the crown who <b>throws yet another tantrum</b> when it is pointed out that her ambassadorial missions were futile.<br /><br />3. A princess of the crown where her family is barely holing the throne who <b>undermines the fragile authority of her brother</b> without a thought. Or two. Scratch that, that’s one thought too many. <br /><br />4. A girl who in spite of points one, two and three <b>believes herself to be “no fool”</b>. Probably this is why she devises a plan that requires posing as a scullery maid. <br /> <br />5. A princess of the crown who <b>takes her own responsibilities so seriously that she leaves the realm without telling anyone</b> and travels with two men of questionable provenance. Unescorted, why not. <br /><br />6. An appointed official taking her responsibilities so seriously that she <b>saunters off when convenient without bothering to notify anyone</b>. Oh, no, scratch that, she did leave a letter. <br /><br />7. A female protagonist <b>constantly comparing herself to other females</b>who are too stupid in her opinion to be interested in anything else beyond their looks, never had ridden a horse, etc. Also, a noble who supposedly has had three maids who dressed and undressed her daily until it was time to impress foreign officials during a diplomatic mission. In that case, check point 1. <br /><br />8. A girl who is quite happy to admit that “she is lousy at being a woman”. Because being a woman equals with good makeup and a love for gossip. You see the problem here?<br /><br />9. A girl who <b>can steer the boat despite never sailing, invents magic spells on the go and leads men to battle before breakfast</b>. Oh, and why don’t you fly an F16 while you’re at it, my dear?<br /><br />10. A girl with <b>penchant for instalove</b> here and there. Just crawl on the bed, she tells her random plebeian sweethearts.<br /><br />11. A girl who <b>gets drunk when on a mission and babbles around all the stupidest things</b> you can imagine.<br /> <br />12. A girl <b>unable to manage one noisy maid and one surly bodyguard suddenly whips out a rebellion</b>.<br /><br />13. A <b>super magician</b> who had no problems with making one person sneeze but scoffs at battle-related specific spells, fancy that. <br /><br />Yes, I could continue this list. <br /><br />There is one honest paragraph about her in book 3, chapter 7. Unfortunately, it was a very brief paragraph and nothing came out of it. In both instalments Arista is <b>more a hindrance and embarrassment than help</b>. The very <b>same mistakes and idiocies repeat chapter in, chapter out</b> and rare moments of lucidity and reflection do not result in a change of action. The only thing that happens is that she evolves into <b>a snowflake with special abilities</b>. <br /><br />OK, I get it: the book is written in a certain convention. Heroes do heroics, while villains die in a villainous way. Everybody behaves themselves accordingly, just as you expect people to behave themselves in a certain way during grandmother’s tea party. It requires specific cliches, stereotypes, and paradoxes in what is usually called a suspension of disbelief. But <b>Arista’s idiocy takes this suspension business to a whole new level</b>. The only saving grace is the fact that she is so stupid that indeed, it is impossible to predict what would she (not) do. <br /><br />It is such a shame that such an awful character managed to spoiler the whole book. Without Arista, or with her kept firmly on the margins of the Riyria adventures, it would have been an altogether pleasant read. I still cannot decide whether the Author knows that Arista is an idiot and winks at me or whether he expects me to take her seriously. <br /><br /><b>I’d love to continue the series hoping for her brutal and untimely death, but I fear that the worst is yet to come.</b><br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />My general rating is a compromise between these two. <br />___<br />Other Riyria Revelations: <br /><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1487377126?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1#comment_form" rel="nofollow noopener">Theft of Swords</a>: The Crown of Conspiracy &amp; Avempartha (#1-2) ★★★★☆<br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2457971300" rel="nofollow noopener">Heir of Novron</a>: Wintertide &amp; Percepliquis (#5-6) ★★★★☆</span>
  <a data-text-id="15377427243437288205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Solseit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57608403-solseit"><img alt="Solseit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501748227p2/57608403.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1701827374?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Solseit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Solseit" href="/user/show/57608403-solseit">Solseit</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1701827374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12509209682280792074">And I know I keep updating this thread today - but I felt inspired and I also made a much longer review of the series!<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://todaysdecameron.wordpress.com/2017/01/10/rise-of-empire-the-riyria-revelations-2-gush-review/'>https://todaysdecameron.wordpress.com...</a><br/>Please let me know your thoughts - and please feel free to suggest any improvements to the review style/blog/any other element! <br/><br/>- - -<br/>I am so impressed by this story - two great thieves facing a scary (because extremely clever) foe. <br/><br/>As you might know, this edition of the book contains two "books" of the story, hence two different plots albei</span>
  <span id="freeText12509209682280792074" style="display:none">And I know I keep updating this thread today - but I felt inspired and I also made a much longer review of the series!<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://todaysdecameron.wordpress.com/2017/01/10/rise-of-empire-the-riyria-revelations-2-gush-review/">https://todaysdecameron.wordpress.com...</a><br />Please let me know your thoughts - and please feel free to suggest any improvements to the review style/blog/any other element! <br /><br />- - -<br />I am so impressed by this story - two great thieves facing a scary (because extremely clever) foe. <br /><br />As you might know, this edition of the book contains two "books" of the story, hence two different plots albeit they continue the same story line (and the general underlying picture) and it is done with finesse so it feels a genuine continuation. <br /><br />The strongest point of this book in my opinion are the characters, specifically Royce and Hadrian who are the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Riyria  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> thieves. They made a profession out of it and they are really good at it. One is more a ruthless and calculating mind, the other is the valiant and honorable warrior who just interact perfectly well together. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ In book 3, Hadrian actually has a very dark moment, he feels lost and he is not doing enough, he feels he is just a common thief taking advantage of situations - the war - and people to make profit. That does not sit well with his conscious and this shows throughout the book. The story though leads to his biggest breakthrough yet when he discovers he is part of a much bigger story, he is the designated body guard of the heir of Novron. This is why he is so good at fighting, skills his father taught him and he developed in a great way.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Arista is one of my favorite female characters lately: She is fierce, strong, independent, educated (because she wanted a higher education) and she becomes stronger and more important than she thinks. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ She has some veiled romance moments, in this book - in both stories - but I think this will lead to the best moment yet, when I hope Hadrian will become her partner! Also, how cool is she, mastering the art of sorcery. Sure, she might be a little too overpowered by creating her own magic but I will leave it as she is blessed and she knows what she is doing, besides the fact that she is slowly getting to know her abilities  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Also, she is spoiled but she is extremely down to earth and she will also find out what that means! <br /><br />The second story just made me happy <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ from sailing to gladiators  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and made me appreciate how scary the foe really is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ an old friend of Royce and a true villain, with a lot of brains!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />We also find new (good) characters and I loved Amilia, she is just so genuine and a great care giver. She really puts it all out and it shows. I want to have an Amilia in my life. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And we also loose Esrahaddon and that was a shocking moment for me. Although it launches Arista in mission impossible mode.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Finally, I genuinely think this book is rich in violence - not grim dark but there is assassination, killings, uprising, gore description of brutality, attempted rape; so far from light topics - but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2063919.Michael_J__Sullivan" title="Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael J. Sullivan</a> delivery of the characters, the dialog and the descriptions just add a lighter tone to the telling which makes this book even more magnetic than already is with the cool stuff happening to the main characters! So, great work of fantasy, I would go as far as to say that anyone would love this series, it is one of those books which can be easily read and loved by every fantasy reader.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15981864945251447395">The Littlefingerising of Fantasy plots has now reached pox levels. I shudder to think what the landscape will look like when it will feel like the plague.<br/><br/>I'm sorry, but there is too much gristle in this book. The rest had Mat</span>
  <span id="freeText15981864945251447395" style="display:none">The Littlefingerising of Fantasy plots has now reached pox levels. I shudder to think what the landscape will look like when it will feel like the plague.<br /><br />I'm sorry, but there is too much gristle in this book. It's perfect length should have been 500 pages at most. I'm not immune to the charms of an adventure on a ship, but even GoT book 5, A Dance With Dragons runs rings round this book using Tyrion's little legs.<br /><br />Oh and the only death that caught me unawares was [name redacted]. The rest had Matsusaka Wagyu stamped all over them. The good bits were often worth reading, but too much is too much.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2625422514198000553">First book felt like a very long build up. Altough I enjoyed learning about the pasts of Hadrian and Royce immensely and wanted more of it, I've felt impatient time to time. I love to hate having opposing feelings<i>*let the mud wrestling begin*</i>. And vice versa. <i>I adore the term vice versa. it has this making sense while not making sense thing going on with it's meaning and the actual sounding of it. sneaky</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481843055ra/21460879.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Alric still seems to be an annoying twat but Arista has come a long way. Actually, if you thi</span>
  <span id="freeText2625422514198000553" style="display:none">First book felt like a very long build up. Altough I enjoyed learning about the pasts of Hadrian and Royce immensely and wanted more of it, I've felt impatient time to time. I love to hate having opposing feelings<i>*let the mud wrestling begin*</i>. And vice versa. <i>I adore the term vice versa. it has this making sense while not making sense thing going on with it's meaning and the actual sounding of it. sneaky</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481843055ra/21460879.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alric still seems to be an annoying twat but Arista has come a long way. Actually, if you think about the forced journey Alric took in the Theft of Swords and Arista's journey in this book, the differences between their maturity levels are obvious. Alric was like an condescending pubescent having a temper tantrum <i>*still is*</i> while Arista is shedding her entitled upbringing and maturing. Especially in the second book!<br><br>Long story short, Alric sucks!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481843055i/21460880.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I've come to respect Arista in the end of the second book. She has become into a strong, complex and quite lovable female character. I stumbled upon this picture on pinterest as a representation of her ;<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481843055i/21460881.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And I think it fits, especially with the darker feeling of the second book. It was grimmer than all of the books before and unpredictable .<i>*at least for me. and that ending!!!*</i><br><br> <blockquote>"Have you ever been in love, Hadrian?”<br>“I’m not sure. How do you tell?”<br>“Love? Why, it’s like coming home.”<br>Hadrian considered the comment.<br>“What are you thinking?” Bulard asked.<br>Hadrian shook his head. “Nothing.”<br>“Yes, you were. What? You can tell me. I’m an excellent repository for secrets. I’ll likely forget, but if I don’t, well, I’m an old man in a remote<br>jungle. I’m sure to die before I can repeat anything.”<br>Hadrian smiled, then shrugged. “I was just thinking about the rain.” </blockquote><br><br>If that means what I think it means <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I smell a couple!! luuuurve is in the air *maniacal dancing* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I approve that message!!!<br><br>Oh, and that ending! I sure wasn't expecting it! Delicious! No, I mean it was sad and I had feelies that punched me in the stomach and a healthy dose of fear for the future, but the unexpectedness of it was delightful.<br><br>First book was 4 stars and the second one 5. Of course I've rounded it up, because it just was awesome!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1926366779" />
    <a title="Orient" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43587353-orient"><img alt="Orient" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500791761p2/43587353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1926366779?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Orient" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Orient" href="/user/show/43587353-orient">Orient</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=recs-by-ivan">recs-by-ivan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=killer">killer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1926366779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15740977608798893632"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489093132i/22185350._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Great books read: 1<br/>Hours spent cheering for the goodies:2462621<br/>Hours spent cheering for the baddies:2462621<br/>Monster count: a few adorable goblins.<br/>Temples for Hadrian: O (I know, I know, I must be out of my mind :D)<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398950169ra/9486683.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>“Rise of Empire” contains two books, “Nyphron Rising” and “The Emerald Storm”<br/>I read “Theft of Swords” recently, and now after the second installment finished, I can admit for sure that this read was way more better for me than the first one. I had a slight drag problem starting “Nyphr</span>
  <span id="freeText15740977608798893632" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489093132i/22185350._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Great books read: 1<br>Hours spent cheering for the goodies:2462621<br>Hours spent cheering for the baddies:2462621<br>Monster count: a few adorable goblins.<br>Temples for Hadrian: O (I know, I know, I must be out of my mind :D)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398950169ra/9486683.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>“Rise of Empire” contains two books, “Nyphron Rising” and “The Emerald Storm”<br>I read “Theft of Swords” recently, and now after the second installment finished, I can admit for sure that this read was way more better for me than the first one. I had a slight drag problem starting “Nyphron Rising” as like during my playdate, Riyria Revelations needs some time to hook up completely. “Rise of Empire” offers an increasing sense of danger, not only for the world, but also for the characters in it and it’s great.<br><br>“Nyphron Rising”<br>The first book starts with significant political revolution as the balance between the political parties changes dramatically and offers war as a solution. Of course, Arista, Hadrian and Royce are entertaining like always, but the story offers some new intriguing characters, too :) <br><br>“The Emerald Storm”<br>The second book develops the political scheming further and even drops the famous BFF couple into the waters they haven’t tasted before. I think this helped to give more flesh to the characters and of course added new interesting ones :)<br><br>Characters. Oh my, the main ones have made a great development. Most obvious and striking change touches the new empress. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A dragon slayer turned into a puppet, my heart still aches for her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Also the story of the little Cinderella, her progress was quick. Her character is definitely well written with all the flaws and innocence, like a sponge, trying to drink all the colors of life. But the thing that hooked me up and kept me interested in the story, is the great interaction between Royce and Hadrian, their friendship is great. Of course I love Arista, her progress as a leader, magician and woman is amazing. I just remember her in the first installment and I must confess, I wasn’t charmed by her in the very start and didn’t appreciate the way some characters were created in “Theft of Swords”. So it's so awesome that this installment changed my opinion. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also I’m sad that the old Witcher is dead, I liked his character, he was one of the most interesting, not sure good or bad :) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The big evil baddies in the “Rise of Empire” are interesting, too. With their gripping backstories, I loved to follow them and admired their wicked mind. The Super Mario was the most alluring and I was a bit disappointed that I couldn’t have more of him! Hope to satisfy this need later on.<br><br>Wordbuilding. “Rise of Empire”is easy and entertaining to read as long as you wait a bit for the story to take pace. The places were well described, I could imagine all the secret alleys and fascinating buildings. When comparing both installments, I feel like this one was more fleshed out, mature and better organized. There are also gripping and tasty scenes with action, scheming, great fights, moments when I caught myself thinking: no way, how the hell did you do that, Mr. Sullivan. If I had to choose which book in this installment was the best out of the two, I’d choose "The Emerald Storm". As much as I enjoyed "Nyphron Rising", I didn’t quite feel that it matched up with pace, gripping action, although they both have great revelations, interesting character development and yummy scheming. <br><br>Plots and characters make a great collaboration through all the four books I read. There are twists and turns and returning characters that keep me hooked. Riyria Revelations is working like a really well organized clock for me despite some flaws.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489093132ra/22185352.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1896260311" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1896260311" />
    <a title="Esme" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44110461-esme"><img alt="Esme" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1896260311?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Esme" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Esme" href="/user/show/44110461-esme">Esme</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1896260311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1395405094851796761">I liked the first book a lot, but this book is just phenomenal. I loved the war, the battle scenes were immerssive. I really loved Hadrian in the first book, but it was Arista that blew my mind this book. I saw someone say something about Sullivan being "naively sexist" and I can not disagree hard enough, I love the way he's written Arista. Learning about Hadrians back story was nuts, I'm just getting more attached to this odd couple friendship. I tend to gravitate towards strong friendships wit</span>
  <span id="freeText1395405094851796761" style="display:none">I liked the first book a lot, but this book is just phenomenal. I loved the war, the battle scenes were immerssive. I really loved Hadrian in the first book, but it was Arista that blew my mind this book. I saw someone say something about Sullivan being "naively sexist" and I can not disagree hard enough, I love the way he's written Arista. Learning about Hadrians back story was nuts, I'm just getting more attached to this odd couple friendship. I tend to gravitate towards strong friendships with two opposing personalities. it's a trope I'll never get tired of and I even married someone who's my opposite. I can not wait to start the last book. I dot actually have a copy and although I read for 6 hours today I'm debating buying the ebook because I want to keep going. fantastic and fun book!<br /><br />Edit: some thoughts I made on reddit <br /><br />I couldn't help but love Amilia and how sweet and patient she was with "Modina". My aunt actually works with these sorts of patients in a mental hospital and it's amazing how much abuse some of these people go through before they make it to someone who has the patience to help them the right way. Lady Constance made a bigger impression on me because of that. Forced feeding and screaming at patients isn't abnormal, unfortunately. I also love how that was repaid in the speech, which was also pretty deftly done for a mentally abused/warped young girl. <br /><br />The relationship between Royce and Hadrian becomes even more interesting which I adore. One trope I truly doubt I'll ever get tired of is the opposites attract/odd couple pairing. I love with Granny and Nanny, I love it with Royce and Hadrian, and I even married my opposite to keep things interesting :) <br /><br />I really love Arista in this book, I think she was developed really well. <br /><br />I felt the pacing was well done, it speeds up and slows down at the right kind of intervals for me. <br /><br />Since I read Age of Myth first, the way the elves are treated is sort of a mind fuck. It does make me curious about why Gwen and particularly Arista don't really care about their part elven friend. Gwen I can sort of understand given her involvement, but Arista seems to take it in stride as well. <br /><br />The whole thing with Hadrians locket and visiting his home town was interesting as well. It is sort of tropey, backwater kid with a huge secret lineage - but I enjoyed it none the less. <br /><br />There were a few deaths in the book that took me off guard. I guess the story seemed so light hearted I was taken aback when they kicked it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1395405094851796761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
