<div id="review_940731870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/940731870" />
    <a title="Conor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30552336-conor"><img alt="Conor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400278909p2/30552336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/940731870?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Conor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Conor" href="/user/show/30552336-conor">Conor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=awesome-books-are-awesome">awesome-books-are-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=riyria">riyria</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer940731870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14484632945567075097">4.5 Stars <br/><br/>Rise of Empire was a really enjoyable compilation of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6527941.Nyphron_Rising__The_Riyria_Revelations___3_' title='Nyphron Rising (The Riyria Revelations, #3) by Michael J. Sullivan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nyphron Rising</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7815817.The_Emerald_Storm__The_Riyria_Revelations___4_' title='The Emerald Storm (The Riyria Revelations, #4) by Michael J. Sullivan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Emerald Storm</a>, books 3 and 4 in the Riyria series. After a slow start in book 1 this series has really picked up, featuring two likeable protagonists whose characters and backstories were really fleshed out here, a great cast of supporting characters and lots of exciting adventures. This omnibus continues the trend started in book 2 in developing the depth and scope of what was initially a light-hearted fantasy</span>
  <span id="freeText14484632945567075097" style="display:none">4.5 Stars <br /><br />Rise of Empire was a really enjoyable compilation of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6527941.Nyphron_Rising__The_Riyria_Revelations___3_" title="Nyphron Rising (The Riyria Revelations, #3) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Nyphron Rising</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7815817.The_Emerald_Storm__The_Riyria_Revelations___4_" title="The Emerald Storm (The Riyria Revelations, #4) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emerald Storm</a>, books 3 and 4 in the Riyria series. After a slow start in book 1 this series has really picked up, featuring two likeable protagonists whose characters and backstories were really fleshed out here, a great cast of supporting characters and lots of exciting adventures. This omnibus continues the trend started in book 2 in developing the depth and scope of what was initially a light-hearted fantasy adventure to great effect.<br /><br />Nyphron Rising- 4.5 Stars<br /><br />This was a great read, the strongest in the series so far. Our heroes from the previous books, Royce and Hadrian, make a return with all of the badass fight scenes, arduous adventures, dangerous missions and witty dialogue we’ve come to expect. However we also get some great backstory on both men as individuals as well as their partnership. Hadrian returns to the home he ran away in search of adventure when he was 14. In doing so we get some really cool insight into his relationship with his father, his character and how he became the badass swordsman we all know and love. The exploration of Royce’s backstory was perhaps even more intriguing. A scene where Royce watches a young urchin struggling to survive on the streets and thinks back to his own, similar childhood was easily one of the best scenes in the series. <br /><br />We are also introduced to Amilia, a humble servant girl. But this is epic fantasy and following a maid around emptying chamber pots and cleaning floors would be a weak-ass story arc. So we need drama. Enter the Empress formerly known as Trace. After the events of the previous book ‘Modina’ became empress of the New Empire, unfortunately she also lost her mind in the process. After a series of coincidental events Amilia has to walk the tight rope of serving as her minder. If she succeeds an escape from the brutal, thankless life of a servant will be hers. If she fails she will never be heard from again. I found Modina’s intense depression to be seriously jarring given the light hearted tone of the rest of the book, however her interaction with Amilia were heartwarming and moving, especially one scene in particular towards the end <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ where Modina gave a speech to save Amilia’s life  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Amilia’s sections also provided an interesting, if somewhat predictable insight into the nature of the class system in this world. <br /><br />While Amilia’s sections were enjoyable I was frustrated by a lot of this storyline. I thought the fact that Modina, the messianic saviour of humanity and (puppet) ruler of the empire, was kept in a tiny cell didn’t make sense and was only thrown in to make her sections even more depressing and the villains even more evil. I also thought that the whole rise of the new empire storyline was stupid. The church somehow managed to convince every squabbling feudal kingdom in the world to give up their kingdoms within a few months. And the legitimacy of the empire is based entirely on a figure of legend (Modina) who is never seen and whose only claim to actually being that legendary figure are the claims of one deranged priest who claims to have seen her kill a magical monster. And this was apparently enough to make a dozen warring kingdoms give up their independence and join together?<br /><br />I was glad Arista got more screen time in this one although I was somewhat disappointed at how predictable her ‘spoiled princess goes on a quest and learns valuable life lessons’ bit was. Even though it was predictable I still enjoyed her sections and towards the end they became even more gripping as plotlines came together amidst scenes of violence and unexpected tragedy that hadn’t been seen in the series so far and added a darker tone and greater level of suspense than I was used to in this series. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ While I found him to be at times annoyingly perfect and heroic I was still shocked and bummed out by Emery’s death  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />The Emerald Storm- 4 Stars <br /><br />While the Emerald Storm didn’t quite match the standards set by ‘Nyphron Rising’ it was still a great read. The main focus of this one was a perilous quest across the world undertaken by Royce and Hadrian. This was a really enjoyable storyline that introduced some great characters, showed us more of the world and further developed Hadrian’s backstory. For the most part the world building in this series is pretty shallow and typical of the genre and that was what we got here however it was still fun to see our heroes trek through thick jungles, bask in the opulence of mercantile city-states and explore crumbling ruins ala Indiana Jones (Hadrian really needs a lucky hat). I’m not normally a fan of naval stuff and parts of this storyline were very heavy on terminology but I still appreciated what seemed a very well-researched portrayal. Probably my favourite aspect of this storyline was the characters. The main antagonist of this storyline was a despicable fanatic priest, however we were also introduced to Wesley, possibly the best secondary character in this series to date, which is saying a lot (see below). I found Wesley to be a nuanced and brilliantly realized portrayal of an honourable man defending his principals in a place where honour is a weakness as well as a younger brother trying to match his older brother’s brilliance, not out of love of glory but out of duty. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And I was seriously shocked and bummed out by his death, especially as I assumed/hoped he would go on to be a major character in this series.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />On the other hand I found Arista’s storyline frustrating and boring. After being entrusted with the responsibility of leading a city in the previous book Arista decides to drop that responsibility in favour of yet another pointless adventure at the start of this book. This seemed designed to continue the ‘spoiled princess learns life lesson’ plot which is both one of the most overplayed clichés in fantasy and had already been done in the previous book. This was confounded by how stupid and selfish Arista’s reasoning for abandoning the city that loved and relied on her was. The storyline itself was slow and dull without much of note happening and was frustrating in how it interrupted the Hadrian and Royce storyline. That being said towards the end it picked up and some interesting stuff began to happen, but not enough to erase how disappointing this story was as a whole. Meanwhile Amilia’s storyline continued to be pretty interesting, further confirming Amilia as one of my favourite characters, although Modina’s appearances continued to be depressing.<br /><br />The secondary characters in this series are crazy good, possibly the best I’ve ever seen in a fantasy series. Sullivan thinks up brilliant characters then has to leave them out of the next book to make room for more brilliant characters. If I had one complaint about this it would be that I want to see more of my favourite secondary characters from previous books. Prince Alric, Myron the nerdy monk, the brilliant dwarf Magnus are all great characters who I want to see more of. <br /><br />Overall this was another good instalment in a really enjoyable series. While still a fun, light-hearted fantasy at heart each instalment becomes more compelling by raising the stakes for drama and tragedy, developing the world and introducing new characters. I’m really psyched to continue this series and see how it ends.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14484632945567075097" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2078972096" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2078972096" />
    <a title="Liam Degnan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan"><img alt="Liam Degnan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2078972096?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam Degnan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam Degnan" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan">Liam Degnan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180038-liam-degnan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2078972096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3449279037373616641"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"There are no honorable causes. There is no good or evil. Evil is only what we call those who oppose us."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><b>
  <u>Four Stars:✰✰✰✰</u>
</b><br/><br/>What everybody kept telling me about these books was so completely right, and I couldn't be happier, because <b>I absolutely loved this second volume of Riyria Revelations</b>. They should make a "Most Improved" award for writers if only so Michael Sullivan could win the award, because where the first volume left me completely unimpressed, <b>this book turned me into a fu</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3449279037373616641" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"There are no honorable causes. There is no good or evil. Evil is only what we call those who oppose us."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><b>
  <u>Four Stars:✰✰✰✰</u>
</b><br /><br />What everybody kept telling me about these books was so completely right, and I couldn't be happier, because <b>I absolutely loved this second volume of Riyria Revelations</b>. They should make a "Most Improved" award for writers if only so Michael Sullivan could win the award, because where the first volume left me completely unimpressed, <b>this book turned me into a fully committed fan of the series</b>. I'll do my best to explain exactly what changed, and in some ways it's hard because this is actually two books in one, but the improvements I noticed definitely apply to both (although I should say up front that book three was my personal favorite so far). <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Regret was a curse without a cure, except to forget."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Characterization:</u>
</b><br /><br />I'm bringing up characters AGAIN as the first thing worth mentioning in this volume. The characters were my favorite thing about the first two books, and yet <b>somehow, Sullivan managed to improve on something that was already truly excellent</b>. In terms of the main characters, Royce and Hadrian, we really got to experience them as individuals on a much deeper level - beyond just viewing them as a likeable mercenary duo. Sullivan starts to go deeper into their personal history, and we get a more personal side from each of them. In the first book, we get A LOT of banter and overall likeability between the two in the context of their relationship with each other, but this character revealed them both to be outstanding protagonists all in their own right. That added so much to this book, and is what I want and hope for in every book that I read. <br /><br />A common complaint of mine when reading fantasy is <b>the profound lack of good female characters</b> even among some of the more popular fantasy authors today(*coughcough*<b>
  <i>
    <u>BRIANMCCLELLAN</u>
  </i>
</b>*coughcough*). It was an issue I had with the first volume of this series, as well. Out of nowhere though in this book, Sullivan not only introduced my favorite character in the series so far (Amilia &lt;3), but also took characters that were previously an annoying princess and a timid farm girl and <b>turned them into true heroes of this story</b>. And he did it in a way that wasn't unrealistic or far fetched, at all. I felt completely convinced by ALL of the characters in this book. Well done!<br /><br />Characters gets a full five stars, without a doubt.<br /><br />**EDIT: I also feel like I need to comment how good the villains of this book are. Sullivan takes us into the other side of this story, so that we experience the corruption that exists within the religious system of the church as well as some of the criminal empires. I love a good villain, and Sullivan definitely brought his A-Game in this book.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Story &amp; The Writing:</u>
</b><br /><br />The writing quality in the last volume felt completely pedestrian to me. Do you ever read a book that's a debut novel, and somehow it just <i>feels</i> like a debut novel? That's how the first book felt. I really enjoy good writing - part of my love for reading comes from my love for just beautiful, descriptive writing. As an example, Name of the Wind by Rothfuss is an "okay" story at best - what separates it from so many other fantasy books, and the reason it is outrageously popular, is the incredible writing. Good prose can turn a scene that would otherwise be empty and hollow information into something that is beautiful, or heart-wrenching, or both. <br /><br />And while Sullivan's writing still does not fit into the "great" category, for me, he made some huge improvements in this book. There were some moments that genuinely shocked me with the amount of emotion Sullivan packed into them - he really doing a good job of getting you into the head of each of the characters. And he does it in a way that <b>makes you feel what they are feeling</b>, whether it's joy, loss, or anything in between. This really helped me get into the story.<br /><br /><b>And the story got soooo much better</b>. The first volume hinted at the content of this one, but never developed on it enough to get me interested, because the plot of both first books was totally mediocre. Both stories told in this volume, especially book three, were drastic improvements. I feel bad that I can't say more, as I really don't want to spoil it. But there were plenty of unexpected surprises along the way, and the more these books develop, the more I enjoy them. <br /><br />My one major issue, and the reason I took off a full star, is that <b>neither book had a very good or satisfying ending</b>. The climax in both novels felt rushed and a little disappointing. To give an example of what I'm talking about.... if you spend a large portion of the book building anticipation for a battle that's coming, I would really like that battle to last longer than two pages and some weak explanation. Book four was a completely abrupt ending with a very boring middle. I didn't even feel like the story climaxed yet when I finished. So that was a bit of a damper. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>In Conclusion:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Sincere thanks to all of the people who kept telling me to stick with these books</b>. In spite of my issues with the endings, I literally loved both of these books. And most importantly, I <b>
  <i>had so much fun reading them</i>
</b>. I don't think I've actually enjoyed a book like I enjoyed these in quite awhile. I can't wait to get through the final volume, and that's a very, very good omen. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"That's why you shouldn't make vows. The moment you do, fate starts conspiring to shove them down your throat."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />***************<br /><br />Spur of the moment buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller" rel="nofollow noopener">Niki</a> and whoever happens to join us over at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/192999-fantasy-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Buddy Reads</a> =].</span>
  <a data-text-id="3449279037373616641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1349765183" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1349765183" />
    <a title="Jody " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41767362-jody"><img alt="Jody " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558120407p2/41767362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1349765183?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody " href="/user/show/41767362-jody">Jody </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1349765183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10395641703219348400">Another stellar installment in the Riyria Revelations series. I loved every chapter of this book, or should I say both books, as this is a combination of books 3 and 4. Anyway, the way Michael J. Sullivan writes just sucks you right into the world. Forget your surroundings, because you will lose all sense of reality. His descriptions of people, places, and things makes you feel like you are right there with Royce and Hadrian in the middle of the action.<br/> <br/>Book 3, Nyphron Rising, has the dynamic du</span>
  <span id="freeText10395641703219348400" style="display:none">Another stellar installment in the Riyria Revelations series. I loved every chapter of this book, or should I say both books, as this is a combination of books 3 and 4. Anyway, the way Michael J. Sullivan writes just sucks you right into the world. Forget your surroundings, because you will lose all sense of reality. His descriptions of people, places, and things makes you feel like you are right there with Royce and Hadrian in the middle of the action.<br /> <br />Book 3, Nyphron Rising, has the dynamic duo of Royce and Hadrian back in the employ of Princess Arista of Melengar. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[With the empire gaining strength and the threat to Melengar growing, Arista leaves with Royce and Hadrian to seek help from the Nationalists, and their leader Degan Gaunt. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> <br />In Book 4, Emerald Storm, we have Royce and Hadrian acting as sailors to gain employment on a ship by the same name, Emerald Storm. What starts out as a mission to get information about the Empires plans, turns into more than they could have imagined.<br /> <br />Royce and Hadrian both have their moments were they take center stage, but Hadrian seemed to get more attention in both of these stories. We learn more about his past when he was young lad, and his travels before he and Royce teamed up to form Riyria.<br /> <br />Both books are fast paced with twists and turns you don’t see coming until its right in your face. Lots of new characters who help spice up the monologue with their vast personalities. But one of my favorite parts of these books is the humor. Mr. Sullivan has a talent to put a comical aspect into almost any situation. This adds a whole new level of entertainment that makes reading these books so much fun.<br /> <br />If you like adventure, with a side of humor, and extra fast paced action these books are for you. If not, then I believe these books are still for you by sheer entertainment level alone. You are missing out on a great read if you don’t give these books a try. As for me…I’m on to the next chapter in the Riyria Revelations.<br /><br />5 stars ***** <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10395641703219348400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1276005502?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1276005502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11820331130173628514">This is an omnibus of books 3 and 4 in the series. The third follows well on the heels of the big battles and what amounts to a civil war with the installment of a puppet on the throne, with our favorite thieves getting caught up in the travail, with the search for the rightful heir on the way in the fourth book, with plenty of hijinks on the high seas to keep things interesting.<br/><br/>What did I think about them?<br/><br/>They're pretty okay. Granted, I've read a lot of fantasy and a lot of great characters who</span>
  <span id="freeText11820331130173628514" style="display:none">This is an omnibus of books 3 and 4 in the series. The third follows well on the heels of the big battles and what amounts to a civil war with the installment of a puppet on the throne, with our favorite thieves getting caught up in the travail, with the search for the rightful heir on the way in the fourth book, with plenty of hijinks on the high seas to keep things interesting.<br /><br />What did I think about them?<br /><br />They're pretty okay. Granted, I've read a lot of fantasy and a lot of great characters who are thieves, a lot of great wizards, a lot of great treatments of elves in wildly different circumstances, and even a lot of fantasy pirates. What makes this stand out from the rest of them? <br /><br />Well, the writing is decent and consistent and the story arcs follow solidly from book to book, feeling more like a long and comfortable adventure with characters I can settle in with for the long haul. That's basically what I get out of it. It's decent. I'd give this a solid 3.5 stars if I had the option. I'll continue, too, because its good enough to keep my interest. <br /><br />But in general? I do kind of wonder where or if it takes real flight or if it will blow me away.</span>

<div id="review_1873381352" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1873381352" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1873381352?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1873381352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10496875672485291544"><b>Full review now posted!</b><br/><i>Original review can be found at <a href='http://booknest.eu' rel='nofollow noopener'>Booknest</a>.</i><br/><br/>What a way to end the year!<br/><br/>Theft of Swords was the first book I started in 2017. Between all of the new books and authors I stumbled across and became obsessed with, the rest of Riyria somehow got lost in the mix. But I’m so happy to be ending my reading year on such a high note; the wait feels worth it.<br/><br/>I loved Theft of Swords because it was fun and engaging and harkened back to some of the foundations of the fantasy genre. I loved </span>
  <span id="freeText10496875672485291544" style="display:none"><b>Full review now posted!</b><br /><i>Original review can be found at <a href="http://booknest.eu" rel="nofollow noopener">Booknest</a>.</i><br /><br />What a way to end the year!<br /><br />Theft of Swords was the first book I started in 2017. Between all of the new books and authors I stumbled across and became obsessed with, the rest of Riyria somehow got lost in the mix. But I’m so happy to be ending my reading year on such a high note; the wait feels worth it.<br /><br />I loved Theft of Swords because it was fun and engaging and harkened back to some of the foundations of the fantasy genre. I loved the relationship between Hadrian and Royce, and I wanted to know more about who they are and the events that formed them. In this second omnibus, I got some of the information I sought, especially regarding Hadrian. I got more bromance and more moral conflict, which made me happy. Hadrian and Royce aren’t my absolute favorite bromance, because that title will always be reserved for Scott Lynch’s Locke and Jean, but they’re definitely in my top five. I love their development in Rise of Empire, and I can’t wait to see how they further develop in Heir of Novron. <br /><br />Yet again, there is a cast of secondary characters that is absolutely wonderful. The book starts with the introduction of Amilia, a maid in the castle of the new Empress. Through a series of random events, she finds herself promoted from maid to secretary of the Empress, tasked with bringing Modina out of her shell and helping form her into the Empress the Empire believes she should be. Amilia is in over her head, but she is intelligent and diligent and, most importantly, fiercely loyal to her ward.<br /><br />We also meet Wesley, a midshipman aboard the Emerald Storm. Wesley is incredibly straight-laced and can often appear stuck-up, but there’s much more to him. This nobleman turned sailor is the epitome of honor, loyal and honest and fair to a fault. Though his manners may be stilted, he never backs down from making the hard decision, even when it’s not in his personal best interest.<br /><br />But my absolute favorite character in this book is one we met in Theft of Swords: Princess Arista. In Theft of Swords, Arista was interesting but definitely a background character. In Rise of Empire, Arista’s character develops dramatically, taking centerstage even over Hadrian and Royce. In my opinion, she’s the character with the most richness and depth in the entire series, and I can’t wait to see how she further develops in the last omnibus of the series. I’ve read a lot of fantasy, and I have no qualms about saying that Arista Essendon is one of the best developed female characters I’ve come across in the genre.<br /><br />There was one character from the first omnibus who wasn’t present in the second and who I really missed: Myron. He’s the cutest, sweetest cinnamon roll of a man I’ve ever come across, and I wish there was an entire series just about him. However, I’ve been informed by reliable sources that he’ll be more present in Heir of Novron, and I’m thrilled at the prospect of seeing him again.<br /><br />Again, I hate that I waited so long (almost a year!) between reading Theft of Swords and Rise of Empire, but I have no regrets. I was able to end the year with a book that I absolutely love, and I have what I’ve been told is an amazing conclusion to look forward to as my first read of 2018. It’s been a wonderful year, full of fantastic stories and friendships founded on a mutual love of books, and I’m excited to see what the new years brings. <br /><br /><b>Happy New Year, everyone! May your 2018 be incredible, and stuffed to the brim with fabulous books!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10496875672485291544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2671959892" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2671959892" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2671959892?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780748131365" href="/book/show/20411020-rise-of-empire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2671959892" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11310581048477515728"><b>
  <i>"Living has no value—it’s what you do with life that gives it worth.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>This book is as good as the first book. Just like the first book this book is also an omnibus of the third and fourth book (Nyphron Rising and Emerald Storm) of the Riyria Revelations.<br/><br/><br/>This book has lots of actions, more magic than the first one. Amazing female characters and plot. I love the depictions of the fight scenes. A little information was given on Hadrian which contributed a lot to the plot.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“There are no honorab</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText11310581048477515728" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Living has no value—it’s what you do with life that gives it worth.”</i>
</b><br /><br />This book is as good as the first book. Just like the first book this book is also an omnibus of the third and fourth book (Nyphron Rising and Emerald Storm) of the Riyria Revelations.<br /><br /><br />This book has lots of actions, more magic than the first one. Amazing female characters and plot. I love the depictions of the fight scenes. A little information was given on Hadrian which contributed a lot to the plot.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“There are no honorable causes. There is no good or evil. Evil is only what we call those who oppose us.”</i>
</b><br /><br />The world is well depicted and I praise the author for that. Each book is set in a new location and he still wows me. The Emerald Storm book 4 of the series is set on sea, 70% of the book was on sea not land, I really likes the way it was portrayed.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Power rises to the top like cream and dominates the weak with cruelty disguised as—and often even believed to be—benevolence. When it comes to people, there is no other possibility. It’s a natural occurrence, like the weather, and you can’t control either one.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Hadrian and Royce is as crazy as ever. Hadrian is ever. There is a small character development, they both changed for the better I think.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Is this a… stew?” she asked.<br />Royce laughed quietly. “He likes to call it that.”<br />“It’s a dish I learned from Thrace,” Hadrian explained with a reminiscent look on his face. “She’s a much better cook than I am. She did this thing with the meat that—Well, anyway, no, it’s not stew. It’s really just boiled salt pork and vegetables. You don’t get a broth, but it takes away the rancid taste of the salt and softens the meat. And it’s hot. Trust me, you’re going to love it.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Arista is who surprised me in this book. She is so more than a princess. She is brave and courageous, she deserves to rule a kingdom mot her brother.<br /><br />Some other interesting characters are Amelia, Modina and Wesley.</span>

<div id="review_1235622359" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1235622359" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1235622359?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=physical-owned">physical-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=dr-reading-challenge">dr-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1235622359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14150294220343196470"><b>Apr 2016: Reread with the fabulous Buddies Books & Baubles</b><br/><br/>-------------------------------------<br/><b>25 Dec 2015 (audio):</b> Finished reread of Rise of Empire and no surprises here - another upgrade to 5-stars and onto my favourites shelf. Interspersing this reread with the latest prequel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24683898.The_Death_of_Dulgath__The_Riyria_Chronicles___3_' title='The Death of Dulgath (The Riyria Chronicles, #3) by Michael J. Sullivan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Death of Dulgath</a>, highlights how well Michael developed the personalities of Hadrian and Royce at the onset of Riyria and after 12 years of friendship/partnership. <br/><br/>-------------------------------------<br/><b>May 2015 (ebo</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14150294220343196470" style="display:none"><b>Apr 2016: Reread with the fabulous Buddies Books &amp; Baubles</b><br /><br />-------------------------------------<br /><b>25 Dec 2015 (audio):</b> Finished reread of Rise of Empire and no surprises here - another upgrade to 5-stars and onto my favourites shelf. Interspersing this reread with the latest prequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24683898.The_Death_of_Dulgath__The_Riyria_Chronicles___3_" title="The Death of Dulgath (The Riyria Chronicles, #3) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Death of Dulgath</a>, highlights how well Michael developed the personalities of Hadrian and Royce at the onset of Riyria and after 12 years of friendship/partnership. <br /><br />-------------------------------------<br /><b>May 2015 (ebook):</b><br />This is the 2nd omnibus comprising Book 3 and 4 of the Riyria Revelations. I have indicated in my review of the 1st omnibus that the series is showing great promise to go deeper as it progresses, and I was not disappointed at all. I don’t know how this was possible as I believe the books were all written on a stand-alone basis before the omnibus versions came about, but the 2-book bundling just seemed to work perfectly in the way the story progresses, and the titles are just so apt! <br /><br /><b>Nyphron Rising (4.25 stars)</b><br /><br />Third book into the Riyria Revelations and the pace is picking up as the plot thickens. The characters really do start to evolve in this instalment, especially Arista. Female leads are usually not the easiest to write, and there are too many out there whom I just don’t really care for. Arista was an exception to me. She wasn’t portrayed to be overly spoilt nor too aggressive nor ridiculously innocent. Although a fairly predictable arc, I find that her progression and growth in character seemed just right given the circumstances. <br /><br />Hadrian’s back story and relationship with his father was explored further as the duo ventured to his hometown. We also see glimpses of the many layers of Royce’s personality. The scene where Royce watched the a little boy struggling in the streets of Ratibor (where he grew up as an orphan) was quite heart-breaking, as was the one where he confessed to Hadrian the real reason for him holding back on Hadrian’s true identity. So yes, by now I have really warmed up to Royce while still crushing on Hadrian. Both really different characters and I love both of them for different reasons.<br /><br />The introduction of another female character in the form of a scullery maid, Amilia, who was tasked to ‘look after’ the new empress Modina, formerly known as Thrace, provided the necessary yet unorthodox POV into the machinations of the New Empire. <br /><br /><b>Emerald Storm (4.5 stars)</b><br /><br />Wow, I love how this series takes off to greater heights with each and every instalment so far. We get to see more of the world of Elan as our favourite duo travels to southern regions of Delgos and Calis on a ship for which the book is named after.<br /><br />I typically do not enjoy naval settings and sailing jargons often just fly right over my head. However, as Hadrian and Royce are both portrayed as sailing rookies, the reader gets the benefit of some form of ‘education’ such that it’s a lot easier for me to breeze through these sections of the book. <br /><br />We got to see Hadrian’s shadier past when we reached Calis, where he had once gained fame with his fighting skills. I have to say that since Book 1, I was literally dying to see Hadrian use the 2-handed sword on this back (which we later learnt is called a spadone, a knight’s weapon). <br /><br />There is a really amazing secondary character introduced in this book, which I won’t elaborate too much about save for this quote from said character:<br /><br /><i>"My father used to say, ‘A knight draws his sword for three reasons: to defend himself, to defend the weak, and to defend his lord,’ but he always added, ‘Never defend yourself against the truth, never defend the weakness in others, and never defend a lord without honor.’</i> --&gt; RESPECT!<br /><br />The other set of POV came from the female characters, Arista, Modina and Amilia. I have to say that I liked every single one of them (which is very rare) – all strong characters in their own right, yet never overly so. A sense of vulnerability or insecurity still pervades and this makes them believable. Modina is getting back on her feet and Arista, oh my, this princess has truly come to her own. <br /><br />As the plot progresses and the world expands, the overall tone also gets darker. While there are still some pockets of humour, there are more deaths and brutality, and of course, the omnipresent theme in most fantasy books, betrayal. In conclusion, thoroughly enjoyable and addictive, and needless to say, I've started on the next book already.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14150294220343196470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1455330425" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455330425" />
    <a title="Stefan Bach" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24053713-stefan-bach"><img alt="Stefan Bach" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603215087p2/24053713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455330425?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefan Bach" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefan Bach" href="/user/show/24053713-stefan-bach">Stefan Bach</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10803593-rise-of-empire">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455330425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14713590459122433919">In February last year I finished <i>
  <b>The Great Hunt</b>
</i> by <i>
  <b>Robert Jordan,</b>
</i> second book in <i>
  <b>The Wheel of Time</b>
</i> series, determined I will never again pick up anything by this author to read. I acknowledged that it was most imaginative worldbuilding and most detailed magic system, with sufficiently good enough prose, but there were these bits and pieces in his writing that were so irritating I couldn’t stand a second anymore reading those books.<br/><br/>Of course six months later I picked it up again. And </span>
  <span id="freeText14713590459122433919" style="display:none">In February last year I finished <i>
  <b>The Great Hunt</b>
</i> by <i>
  <b>Robert Jordan,</b>
</i> second book in <i>
  <b>The Wheel of Time</b>
</i> series, determined I will never again pick up anything by this author to read. I acknowledged that it was most imaginative worldbuilding and most detailed magic system, with sufficiently good enough prose, but there were these bits and pieces in his writing that were so irritating I couldn’t stand a second anymore reading those books.<br /><br />Of course six months later I picked it up again. And honestly I don’t know what happened in those six months. <br />Did I grew up? Have I went through anger management treatment? <br />Whatever the reason, those problems I had with second book were gone. I found myself utterly mesmerized by his books and today The Wheel of Time series sits in third place on my favorite fantasy series list.<br /><br />Then comes first <i>(two)</i> book<i>(s)</i> in the <i>
  <b>Riyria Revelations</b>
</i> series I finished this January. <br />I wasn’t nearly as much disappointed as with second book in Robert Jordan’s series, and even disappointment I felt I prescribed to first novel and really, really high expectations I had reading reviews of all of those who were praising it.<br />The thing is, all of those who were praising it, have finished first, read second and probably already started third series by this author; they have seen Sullivan’s improvement throughout the books and reacted accordingly.<br /><br />Hence, I did everything that worked with Robert Jordan’s series. <br />I left it <i>‘brewing’</i> for several months, waiting and listening for a sign <i>(send by myself)</i> that will say: <i>Now! Get it now!</i><br />Several days ago, I lowered my expectations, started this book and hoped for the best. Because that’s what you do, when you see your friends being excited for the series, describing it in superlatives and enjoying it. You want to participate.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>So what am I missing here?</b>
</i><br /><br />Book, like previous one, consists out of two books, two separate stories which are mutually intertwined. <br />In those stories is again masterfully written charismatic duo <i>
  <b>Hadrian</b>
</i> and <i>
  <b>Royce.</b>
</i> With addition of exploring character of <i>
  <b>Aristea</b>
</i> even further and finding new favorites like <i>
  <b>Amilia,</b>
</i> seeing her progress, her characterization, speaks to me that I’m dealing with a really talented and capable author who knows what he wants from, and how to write, his characters.<br /><br />But then, there are huge bumps in structural narrative of, let’s say, for an example, a chapter. <br />In almost each chapter, for almost 80% of it, he’s developing story really slow, he drowns you with words, he lulls you with information’s, only to abruptly end with those last 20% of the chapter in adrenaline high speed chase or a decisive battle.<br /><br />There are two problems with this that prevented me from enjoying this book. <br /><br />First is that 80%-20% ratio is highly unbalanced. It confuses me, then it bothers me. <br />Each chapter starts with these characteristics of a <i>‘slower’</i> novel and a slower development, only to end in a high paced thrilling chase. <br />I don’t mind that it’s complete opposite, but I do mind that is so abrupt. And I wouldn’t mind if it was only high paced or only slower development. Or better yet, if it was equally balanced, 50%-50% ratio of both. <br />Just decide and choose one or second, or more balanced both.<br /><br />Second problem is directly deriving from first: as is he doing it with almost every single chapter, after a time, it becomes redundant and repetitive, which leads to unfortunate predictability.<br />Why am I reading this if I already know how will each chapter end? How will story end? Which character is going to die, and how? <br />And it’s all written in it, lay out for us to see, but far, far too obvious.<br /><br />I would dismiss him and wouldn’t consider reading his books in the future if he, for many times, hasn’t done completely opposite to what I am complaining here. Surprised me on dozen occasions where I really didn’t see some things coming.<br /><br />If there wasn’t a brief moment when this world reminded me of that of Robert Jordan’s, when they go into Hadrian’s village, get drunk with townsfolk, and spend the night in a cottage. One rare moment when a chapter doesn’t end with adrenaline filled chase. <br />A breath of fresh air and a moment of peace.<br />But much needed moment for structurally improving everything, adding layers in characterization, making this world seem more real and believable and story feeling closer and more intimate to you.<br /><br />Of course I’m not giving up. I want to see this through. Not just this series but all of them. <br />There’s a talent, there’s a knowledge and he’s clearly capable. I just need to come to the point when I’ll enjoy his books in their entirety.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14713590459122433919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1455330425">

<div id="review_1074779740" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1074779740" />
    <a title="Armina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5600230-armina"><img alt="Armina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346961571p2/5600230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1074779740?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Armina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Armina" href="/user/show/5600230-armina">Armina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10803593-rise-of-empire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5600230-armina?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5600230-armina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5600230-armina?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5600230-armina?shelf=bg">bg</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5600230-armina?shelf=audio-tim-gerard-reynolds">audio-tim-gerard-reynolds</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1074779740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6272350115807149388">Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12571107-desinka' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>Desinka</b>
</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8192509-gavin' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>Gavin</b>
</a><br/><br/><i>
  <b>4 STARS</b>
</i><br/><br/>Just like the first book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_2_' title='Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1-2) by Michael J. Sullivan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Theft of Swords</a>, <b>
  <i>Rise of Empire</i>
</b> is two novels in one: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6527941.Nyphron_Rising__The_Riyria_Revelations___3_' title='Nyphron Rising (The Riyria Revelations, #3) by Michael J. Sullivan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nyphron Rising</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7815817.The_Emerald_Storm__The_Riyria_Revelations___4_' title='The Emerald Storm (The Riyria Revelations, #4) by Michael J. Sullivan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Emerald Storm</a>. Where the first two novels of the first Omnibus could survive as stand alone stories, tied together with similar backdroppings and continuing elements, <i>Rise of Empire</i> has moved deep into the connecting plot.<br/><br/>In <b>
  <i>Nyphron Rising</i>
</b>, the newly formed Empire, which the Nyphron Church is running in all but name, would like to anne</span>
  <span id="freeText6272350115807149388" style="display:none">Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12571107-desinka" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Desinka</b>
</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8192509-gavin" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Gavin</b>
</a><br /><br /><i>
  <b>4 STARS</b>
</i><br /><br />Just like the first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_2_" title="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1-2) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Theft of Swords</a>, <b>
  <i>Rise of Empire</i>
</b> is two novels in one: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6527941.Nyphron_Rising__The_Riyria_Revelations___3_" title="Nyphron Rising (The Riyria Revelations, #3) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Nyphron Rising</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7815817.The_Emerald_Storm__The_Riyria_Revelations___4_" title="The Emerald Storm (The Riyria Revelations, #4) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emerald Storm</a>. Where the first two novels of the first Omnibus could survive as stand alone stories, tied together with similar backdroppings and continuing elements, <i>Rise of Empire</i> has moved deep into the connecting plot.<br /><br />In <b>
  <i>Nyphron Rising</i>
</b>, the newly formed Empire, which the Nyphron Church is running in all but name, would like to annex Melengar. Thrace, the young woman from the previous book, has been named the Heir of Novron and is rechristened as the Empress Modina. But Modina is a puppet, existing in a state of almost zombie-like shock. Sullivan reveals more about Royce and Hadrian and their backstories in this third novel and brings the princess Arista more into the spotlight. Arista in particular is becoming quite resourceful. I loved her new confident and becoming-pro "Art" personality. The assistant of the new Empress Modina, Amilia, was a great addition to the story as well. In short, Sullivan is beginning to expand his series from individual character sword &amp; sorcery to larger scale stories, and I found this mix of traditional ingredients of epic fantasy with compelling storytelling to be very appealing.<br /><b>Rating</b>: 4.5 stars<br /><br />The fourth book, <b>
  <i>The Emerald Storm</i>
</b>, takes its title from the ship on which Royce and Hadrian find themselves for much of the novel. Sullivan splits the time between the adventure at sea with the continuing development of the bond between Modina and her assistant Amilia, Modina’s emergence from her shell, and Amilia’s growing respectability in the court. Arista arrives with news that the true heir, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Degan Gaunt <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, survives somewhere. This is a much darker book with bits of heavy foreshadowing. The final pages come much sooner than you expect, leaving you on a rather significant cliffhanger. It's good I can start the next book immediately.<br /><b>Rating</b>: 4 stars<br /><br />On a more personal note, it took me a lot of time to read this book. But not because it was not enjoyable! The reason was that I almost interrupted my reading because of another book I started unexpectedly and needed to finish faster. Despite this interruption or rather because of it I could appreciate the quality of <b>
  <i>Rise of Empire</i>
</b> even more. I would define it as a comfort read. It's enjoyable and satisfying no matter when/how/how much you read it. Recommended! </span>
  <a data-text-id="6272350115807149388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1743405705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1743405705" />
    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23206148-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473945175p2/23206148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1743405705?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terence" href="/user/show/23206148-terence">Terence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1743405705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16237286018103046338"><b>
  <u>Nyphron Rising</u>
</b><br/><br/>With a newly declared heir, the Nyphron Empire looks to gain control over everyone. Melengar stands alone against the growing colossus and Princess Arista has a desperate plan. She defies her brother, hires Riyria, and plans on forging an alliance with the Nationalist Army. Meanwhile Royce debates telling Hadrian about what Esrahaddon showed him in the tower of Avempartha. Royce doesn't trust the Wizard and first intends on learning the truth to the claims by investigating Hadr</span>
  <span id="freeText16237286018103046338" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Nyphron Rising</u>
</b><br /><br />With a newly declared heir, the Nyphron Empire looks to gain control over everyone. Melengar stands alone against the growing colossus and Princess Arista has a desperate plan. She defies her brother, hires Riyria, and plans on forging an alliance with the Nationalist Army. Meanwhile Royce debates telling Hadrian about what Esrahaddon showed him in the tower of Avempartha. Royce doesn't trust the Wizard and first intends on learning the truth to the claims by investigating Hadrian's past.<br /><br />Nyphron Rising is a solid continuation of the tale of Riyria Revelations. I enjoy the story overall, but from time to time the tropes are a heavy weight for me. The antagonists are incredibly evil while the heroes are good for goods sake...except for Royce, he does what he does for profit.<br /><br />The main strength of the series remains for me as Royce and Hadrian. They are an unlikely duo yet I cheer for them, particularly Hadrian, to succeed. They are two men whose actions are far more important than most realize.<br /><br />Nyphron Rising was good and I wonder what will happen next as the story continues.<br /><br />3.5 out of 5 stars<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Emerald Storm</u>
</b><br /><br />A message is intercepted regarding Merrick Marius's plans. King Alric tasks Royce and Hadrian to find out what Marius is up to which leads to them boarding the Emerald Storm. Meanwhile Princess Arista has left Ratibor in search of the true Heir of Novron.<br /><br />I had a little bit of trouble with The Emerald Storm largely because much of the story revolves around Royce and Hadrian's travels on a ship. It's full of all the seaman jargon which honestly bores me. Once the duo left the high seas though the story was excellent.<br /><br />Arista's story was equally strong as she taps deeper into her magical powers and performs some remarkable feats. Arista has demonstrated the most growth of any character in the series and I look forward to how her story continues.<br /><br />One thing I find I dislike about the series thus far is a lot of time is spent with the characters traveling. When something particularly poignant is happening this doesn't bother me, but to show traveling for traveling sake is frustrating at times.<br /><br />The Emerald Storm is likely my favorite story of the series thus far and it has me excited to read the final omnibus of the series.<br /><br />4 out of 5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="16237286018103046338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1074440737" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1074440737" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1074440737?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1074440737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer363686050836225872">This was an omnibus containing both <i>Nyphron Rising</i> and <i>The Emerald Storm</i>. <br/><br/><b>Nyphron Rising</b><br/><br/>This was a fast paced and exciting read. Royce and Hadrian were at their witty best as they accompanied Arista on a diplomatic mission to seek allies against the Imperialists. <br/><br/>I felt Arista really grew and developed into a strong character over the course of this story. <br/><br/>We had a new POV character in the form Amelia. She was the companion of the new Empress Modina. Her storyline was pretty interesting. <br/><br/>Rating </span>
  <span id="freeText363686050836225872" style="display:none">This was an omnibus containing both <i>Nyphron Rising</i> and <i>The Emerald Storm</i>. <br /><br /><b>Nyphron Rising</b><br /><br />This was a fast paced and exciting read. Royce and Hadrian were at their witty best as they accompanied Arista on a diplomatic mission to seek allies against the Imperialists. <br /><br />I felt Arista really grew and developed into a strong character over the course of this story. <br /><br />We had a new POV character in the form Amelia. She was the companion of the new Empress Modina. Her storyline was pretty interesting. <br /><br />Rating 4.5 stars. <br /><br /><b>The Emerald Storm</b><br /><br />I was less happy with this book. It was not as fast paced or as humorous as the previous three books in the series. The time Hadrian and Royce spent on the titular ship, The Emerald Storm, was a bit boring. <br /><br />Arista's storyline was a bit hit and miss. I liked some bits and not others. Amelia suffered badly in this book. Her storyline was boring as she came off as a bit annoying in the later stages of the book. <br /><br />The ending provided some interesting developments so hopefully things will pick up again in the fifth book.<br /><br />Rating: 3.5 stars. <br /><br />Audio Note: Tim Gerard Reynolds continues as narrator. He would be a good narrator if it was not for his awful accents choices. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="363686050836225872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

So, again, this r</span>
  <span id="freeText183963775732280983" style="display:none">I accidentally deleted my GR review!! 😱😱😱 Thank God I had a backup somewhere!<br><br><b>You can find <a href="http://novelnotions.net/2018/10/01/rise-of-empire-the-riyria-revelations-3-4/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> review and more at <a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a>. </b><br><br><i>Beware this review contains one spoiler from Theft of Swords.</i><br><br><b>Rise of Empire was definitely the turning point for me, where I finally saw all the potential of the series and so I knew from the first chapters that this would be a favorite series after all.</b><br><br>Just like Theft of Swords, Rise of Empire includes two books: Nyphron Rising and The Emerald Storm. So, again, this review will be divided into two parts.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488300147i/22099833._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Fanart by <a href="http://sarctic.deviantart.com/art/Riyria-384991614" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarctic</a></i><br><br><br><b>
  <u>Nyphron Rising</u>
</b><br>The events of the first book take place a few months after Avempartha. Arista, princess of Melengar trusts Riyria with a new delicate mission, while the new Empire is spreading, threatening her kingdom and gaining power, influence and territory.<br><br>I left Arista from my review of Theft of Swords on purpose because I knew that I will rave about her in this one. Arista is the type of female character I LOVE to read about in Fantasy. <b>Flawed and far from being perfect, stubborn, loyal, clever and most importantly always evolving, growing, doubting, learning.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“She’s becoming more human every day,” Hadrian said, smiling at her.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Michael has a unique talent at writing astonishing and well fleshed out female characters.</b> All the female POVs were different, with distinctive voices and providing a lot of insight into the ladies' thoughts and doubts and memories. I was enthralled by their chapters as they made a difference and actively took part in the events surrounding them. But they also introduced and interacted with many interesting and amazing side characters: Ibis, Nimbus, Emery, Hintindar's villagers...<br><br>In Rise of Empire, Hadrian shares the favorite spot with Arista (and has ascended to my top 3 of favorite character of all time since my first read). <b>Hadrian is the embodiment of the type of hero I crave to see in epic Fantasy: honorable, idealistic, honest, good-natured and loyal to a fault.</b> I loved getting to know more about his past, his motivations and his lineage. I loved to have more introspection in his POVs where regrets and dreams intertwined and gave birth to one obsession : finding and fulfilling a noble goal.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>When I was young, I used to think I was … well … special. I imagined that I would triumph in some great purpose, win the girl, and save the kingdom, but I suppose every boy feels that way.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>But Nyphron Rising's strength doesn't reside only in its amazing cast but also and foremost in the way the mystery and plot considerately thickened and became more complex as <b>political scheming and battle tactics finally gained in importance and the stakes rose considerably.</b><br><br><b><u>The Emerald Storm</u> </b><br>A huge part of the Emerald Storm takes place on a ship. God, I hate ships in books! But this is really an "<b>It's not you, it's me</b>" situation. First, the ships and sailing jargon confuses me so much and second, the action space is considerably reduced while I love open spaces and huge castles and endless forests and countryside in my Fantasy.<br><br>However, the story is really compelling in this book. More great supporting characters and mysterious and uncanny antagonists were added to the cast. Though it's divided into 3 main storylines (Arista, Amelia &amp; Modina, Hadrian &amp; Royce), I felt the book was more focused on Royce this time which is great because we finally get a clear glimpse of his dark side. Hadrian's memories continue to be told and it's a pleasure to delve into his past and know more about him. The two partners continue to banter and have each other back and each book, reminds me why they form my favorite duo in Fantasy!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You aren’t going to tell me, are you?”<br>“What would be the fun in that? This will give you something to do. You can try to guess, and I can amuse myself by insulting your intelligence.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Conclusion </b><br>These books are a delight to read and re-read as they definitely get better and more exciting with each installment and we get to guess that there are other secrets and mysteries waiting to be unraveled! I even managed to get surprised by some twists I totally forgot about during my re-read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="183963775732280983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_221238724" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221238724" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/221238724?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221238724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5930681235159631070">Rise of Empire is the second omnibus of The Riyria Revelations, containing books three and four, Nyphron Rising and The Emerald Storm, in the six book series. <br/><br/>These two books step things up to a new level and I'm excited to see how this will all end. I still can't believe these were independently published and then republished by such as Orbit. They are definitely deserving.<br/><br/><br/><b>Nyphron Rising</b><br/><br/>At the end of Avempartha, the Nyphronian church decided that the "heir," and therefore emperor (or empress as</span>
  <span id="freeText5930681235159631070" style="display:none">Rise of Empire is the second omnibus of The Riyria Revelations, containing books three and four, Nyphron Rising and The Emerald Storm, in the six book series. <br /><br />These two books step things up to a new level and I'm excited to see how this will all end. I still can't believe these were independently published and then republished by such as Orbit. They are definitely deserving.<br /><br /><br /><b>Nyphron Rising</b><br /><br />At the end of Avempartha, the Nyphronian church decided that the "heir," and therefore emperor (or empress as is the case) would be decided by the person who slayed the monster, the Gyleyreyerezxffv (sp). :)<br /><br />Instead of actually following their plan, the church decided instead to put up a pawn who could easily be controlled. That's just easier right?<br /><br />Nyphron Rising takes us directly from Avempartha and into the life of the now Empress (and almost mute) Modina who was formerly the girl Thrace, who we saw in Avempartha.<br /><br />This book does a lot of setting up for the novels to come. While it is a stand-alone and has a great and exciting ending, the majority of the book is filled with character development and a number of answers to the mysteries presented in earlier volumes.<br /><br />Now, that may sound like a bit of a downer, Sullivan's writing is the same fast-paced style that keeps you turning pages. Admittedly, this will not be known as my favorite in the series, it continues to be a great installment in an amazing series. Nyphron Rising is a necessary book that takes the series to a whole new level and I'm sure it will pay off in the long run.<br /><br />4 out of 5 Stars (Highly Recommended)<br /><br /><br /><b>The Emerald Storm</b><br /><br />Our favorite thieves, Royce and Hadrian, are considering calling it quits, but with the discoveries Hadrian has made, there's no way he can give up just yet. And we all know Royce can't keep his hand out of the cookie jar either.<br /><br />The Emerald Storm was the right book at the right time for me. We just had the twins, moved a couple states away, and I was tired to say the least. This book was amazing and my favorite in the series so far.<br /><br />A note is intercepted from Royce's arch-nemesis, Merrick, who is working for the church and their allies. This leads them on a voyage on The Emerald Storm where Royce and Hadrian have to convince the crew to even let them on...and they are not sailors in any way, shape, or form.<br /><br />I have to admit, my favorite parts involved Hadrian and Royce on the ship, I just can't resist a good nautical-themed story. (I still have nautical-themed birthdays...I wish).<br /><br />Again, Sullivan's writing keeps you turning the pages. It's not as immersive as some books I've read and usually prefer, but it's the perfect style for lots of good fun. And sometimes you get tired of being immersed. When you do, this is the type of series that just hits the spot.<br /><br />4 out of 5 Stars (Highly Recommended)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5930681235159631070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jnPmmFKTnbu4N7Shgps/ZX0hQW0pSs6aLBILNcWivJVafgGm0dqCW0UJdKkNc8HI3Y4YacvD+dcZpBg4PAz+uw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('q34yRbbKUBRQncalVUHA775sDlylmRfw9EK3Ypjhg0F/c9V7NYNP9K2jBq3aqT5CHsNXWEcQIL3B9KRvYU/Bbw==')})
  }

As chaos and civil war begin to overtake the country, Falcio has precious little time left to stop those determined to destroy his homeland.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"1084565419671342861\"
